The email trail also contains the earlier mediation-related discussions from August 2025. Max Smith’s August 26, 2025 message explicitly asked for proposed mediators so that dates could be secured, with a preference for Pete Palmer or Larry Church, while expressing openness to other options. Deborah’s August 25 message regarding Dr. Edelson’s IME invoice and the August 7 and August 5 messages about the Agreed Order show concurrent steps toward settlement tactics and case management.

Throughout these exchanges, the emails include external-email banners, reflecting that some communications originated from outside the recipient’s organization. On June 25, 2025, at 10:25:25 AM Eastern Time, an email was forwarded that began with an instruction to Faye Gaither to draft a letter on letterhead for Mo’s [DOB-63] case and then forward it to a specified recipient. The sender, Aaron Whaley, addressed Faye and Muhammad Alif’s Filevine project email, asking that the letter be prepared in a formal letter format on letterhead and then sent to the person listed below. The forwarded message contained a draft letter beginning with “To Whom It May Concern,” noting that Whaley Whaley Law Firm represents the client in connection with treatment for injuries from an automobile accident that occurred on March 9, 2025. The draft letter expresses gratitude for the treating provider’s flexibility regarding the financial aspects of medical treatment, explaining that automobile accident victims are often financially strained due to the negligent party’s and/or the responsible party’s insurer’s failure to accept responsibility and pay for reasonable and necessary medical treatment. It notes that an insurance adjuster may request medical records to settle a clear liability claim and asks for cooperation in providing those records and the associated bills.

The letter further states that the law firm will protect the unpaid balance for the client’s medical care and treatment “out of and to the extent of net proceeds of any settlement or monetary recovery from the negligent third-party.” It defines “net proceeds” as the gross settlement amount less payment of attorney’s fees and attorney’s expenses. The letter also clarifies that it is not a guarantee of payment, but rather acknowledges and respects the recipient’s agreement to provide necessary medical treatment and to wait to be paid until the case resolves.

Earlier in the thread, there was a sequence of communications about obtaining a formal Letter of Protection (LOP). On April 21, 2025, Lisset Abundis, the LOP Liaison, emailed Aaron Whaley, Sarena Tuttle, and Muhammad Alif’s Filevine address, requesting a formal letter of protection on letterhead that reads your firm will pay for services rendered. This message also contained the Kentucky Court of Justice confidentiality notice.

Throughout the thread, standard confidentiality and privilege notices were included in the emails, including explicit warnings not to read or forward communications if the recipient was not the intended addressee. Since Mediation failed and the Defense Counsel's position, I do not anticipate any resolution prior to that date. In an email titled FW: Muhammad Alif MVA 11/08/22, Lisa Jewell wrote to Sarena Tuttle, “Good afternoon, I just spoke with the adjuster on this case, and I was told that this case was closed, and benefits were already released a while ago, by the attorney. No one relayed that information in any of the emails I have sent. Benefits are now exhausted. I have requested an exhaust letter. Once I have that letter, balance will be moved to lien.” This message was sent on Wednesday, March 26, 2025, at 16:20:40 +0000.

Additional contextual details from the threads include that the July 8, 2024 email chain referenced a PIP (Personal Injury Protection) reservation due to ongoing litigation, with multiple providers potentially claiming PIP benefits; the defense’s willingness to settle or proceed to trial would influence how any available funds would be allocated. By November 2024, the case had advanced toward trial, with a firm trial date set for June 3, 2025, and an expectation that no resolution would occur before that date, absent an unexpected development. By March 2025, communication indicated the case status had shifted to a closed/ Exhausted-terminated state per the adjuster, prompting the request for an exhaust letter and plans to move the remaining balance to lien upon receipt of that letter. Over the period from July 2024 through March 2025, communications between Lisa Jewell of Aptiva Health and Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm tracked the status of Mr. Muhammad Alif’s workers’ compensation claim arising from a motor vehicle accident on [DOB-2555], and the management of related PIP benefits. Tuttle as a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, located at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with D: [PHONE-314], O: [PHONE-315] ext 104, and email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (note: new email address noted in the message). On July 8, 2024, Lisa Jewell wrote that Farmers had advised benefits were being reserved because the patient was no longer treating, and she requested permission to release those benefits, attaching an itemization for review. Sarena Tuttle replied later that day, stating that the PIP reservation could not be removed at that time because Mr. Alif’s claim was in litigation and involved multiple providers who would eventually claim the PIP benefits. She explained that once a determination was made whether the Defense would settle or whether the matter would proceed to trial, they would have a clearer understanding of how the funds should be divided. She advised Lisa to diary a 90- to 120-day follow-up to check back in.

Earlier in the chain, on November 7, 2024, Lisa Jewell sent a message asking for an update and whether benefits could be released yet. In response, Sarena Tuttle sent a message at 11:38 AM on the same day (addressed to Lisa) explaining that the claim was moving to trial, with Trial set for June 3, 2025. She noted that mediation had failed and that the Defense Counsel’s position made any resolution unlikely before the trial date, promising to provide updates should anything unexpected occur.

That same day, November 7, 2024 at 11:29 AM, Lisa had previously asked, “Do you have an update on this case? Can benefits be released yet?” which precipitated the subsequent reply from Sarena.

Earlier still, on July 8, 2024 at 12:42 PM, Lisa had written that Farmers had advised benefits were being reserved because the patient was no longer treating and asked whether benefits could be released, attaching an itemization for review. Sarena responded at 1:31 PM that day, explaining that the PIP reservation could not be removed at that time because the claim was in litigation and involved multiple providers who would ultimately claim the PIP benefits. She reiterated that a determination about settlement versus trial would clarify how funds should be allocated and suggested checking back in after 90–120 days.

Most recently, on March 26, 2025, at approximately 12:20 PM, Lisa stated in an email that she had spoken with the adjuster who claimed the case had been closed and that benefits had already been released some time ago by the attorney, that no one had relayed this information in prior emails, and that benefits were exhausted. She requested an exhaust letter and indicated that once the letter was received, the balance would be moved to lien.

Sarena Tuttle replied at 12:47 PM the same day with a corrective clarification: while the claim may appear “closed” to the adjuster because the claim had moved into litigation, the claim itself remained viable and set for Trial. She emphasized that no benefits had been released to date, to her knowledge.

In summary, the Muhammad Alif MVA case remains active and is scheduled for Trial on June 3, 2025, with mediation having failed previously. PIP benefits have not been released to date, and discussions about benefit allocation depend on whether the defense settles or the case proceeds to trial. The communications include multiple inquiries about benefit releases and the legal status of the claim, as well as updates from The Whaley Law Firm indicating ongoing litigation and forthcoming trial-related actions.

Re: Muhammad Alif 11/8/22 accident. On May 9–10, 2024, the Whaley Law Firm team conducted internal communications regarding discovery in the Muhammad Alif 11/8/22 accident case. The thread began with an email from Sarena M. The eFiling included a document titled “NOTICE OF SERVICE.” For additional details, you can view the filing via the Kentucky Court of Justice eFiling dashboard at https://kcoj.kycourts.net/efiling/Dashboard/Receipt?caseid=6662209 or view the document itself at https://kcoj.kycourts.net/eFilingRetrieval/Home/Package?id=4B648768-CB75-44DE-B793-899CF81B1BB7. This message was automatically generated by the Kentucky Court of Justice eFiling system, and the sender requests that recipients not reply.

A confidentiality notice from the Kentucky Court of Justice accompanies this message. It states that the message and any attachments are intended only for the addressee and may contain privileged, confidential, and/or proprietary work product. If you are not the intended recipient or an authorized representative of the intended recipient, you should not read, copy, retain, or disseminate the message or its attachments, and you should not forward them without the sender’s express written consent. If you have received the message in error, you should contact the sender immediately and delete all copies of the message and any attachments. item_370.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-1716]
Client: Muhammad Alif

In August 2023, the Whaley Law Firm’s file concerning Muhammad Alif, whose motor vehicle accident case is dated [DOB-1717], included a running email thread about a prescription approval for his medication. On August 7, 2023, Sarena Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm (address: 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-1718]; O: [PHONE-1719] ext 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com; note: this is a new email address), forwarded to Aaron Whaley an email titled “Prescription Approval Request Form - Muhammad Alif.” In that forwarded message, she wrote: “Apparently Mo's Medication is actually $3000.00 not $1000.00 - Need new approval form.” This included the context that the medication cost had changed and a new approval form was required.

Earlier in the thread, on August 4, 2023, Brenda Juarez, LOP Dept. Manager at ASP Cares (address: 13988 Diplomat Dr. Suite 100, Farmers Branch, TX 75234; P: [PHONE-1720]; D: [PHONE-1721]; Fax: [PHONE-1722]; [EMAIL-1723]; [EMAIL-1724]; corporate payments to: ASP Cares, 13988 Diplomat Dr. Suite 100, Farmers Branch, TX 75234), responded to the matter. In a message dated August 4, 2023 at 4:13 PM, she stated that there had been confusion on their part and that the medication cost is $3,000.00 with no reduction. She invited any questions and provided her contact number [PHONE-1725]) and noted the updated approval form attached. She also included the ASP Cares office information and the confidentiality statement common to their emails. Earlier that same day, at 12:08 PM, Sarena Tuttle had written to Brenda: “Please find attached the Requested LOP Rx Approval Form.” Brenda later replied with a brief “Thank you!” at 12:29 PM.

The email chain began with Sarena Tuttle’s guidance on billing and prescription handling. On August 1, 2023 at 1:07 PM, Sarena wrote: “Thank you for reaching out. Please bill Mr. Alif's private health insurance for this medication.” Later that afternoon, at 4:10 PM, the LOP Department responded: “We have not filled any medication for the patient yet. We are still waiting on the LOP.” The following day, August 2, 2023 at 8:56 AM, Sarena stated: “Good morning, We have advised that you should bill the patients health insurance for these medications.” At 11:18 AM that day, the LOP Department replied: “We will have the medication transferred out to their local pharmacy.”

Thus, the thread shows a sequence of steps: initial instruction to bill private health insurance, acknowledgment that no medication had been filled yet while awaiting the LOP, the plan to transfer the medication to the local pharmacy, and finally the September/early August exchange preparing for an updated LOP Rx Approval Form reflecting the $3,000 cost.

Amid these exchanges, the correspondence consistently included standard confidentiality notices. The final note in the chain, dated August 7, 2023, is a forward of Sarena’s earlier message to Aaron Whaley with the line about the medication costing $3,000 and the need for a new approval form. The thread thus documents ongoing coordination between The Whaley Law Firm and ASP Cares regarding Muhammad Alif’s LOP medication, including cost updates, billing instructions to private health insurance, and the processing of the LOP Rx Approval Form.

item_371.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-1727]. Client: Muhammad Alif.

In August 2023, a sequence of email communications concerned a high-cost prescription for Muhammad Alif, related to his motor vehicle accident (MVA) case. The correspondence involved Brenda Juarez, LOP Department Manager at ASP Cares, and Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm. The discussion centered on obtaining approval to dispense the medication and on billing arrangements.

The thread began on July 31, 2023, when the LOP Department noted that the patient’s prescription was high-cost and would require approval before dispensing. The note also stated that due to the high cost, they could not accept an unspecified option that was left incomplete in the original message. On August 1, 2023 at 1:07 PM, Sarena advised that Mr. Alif’s private health insurance should be billed for the medication. Later that same day, at 4:10 PM, the LOP Department replied that they had not yet filled any medication for the patient and were still waiting on the LOP.

The following day, August 2, 2023, at 8:56 AM, Sarena reiterated the recommendation to bill the patient’s private health insurance for the medications. Then at 11:18 AM, the LOP Department stated that they would have the medication transferred out to the patient’s local pharmacy. By August 4, 2023, the communications included a note from Sarena indicating that the requested LOP Rx Approval Form had been attached.

On August 4, 2023 at 12:08 PM, Sarena again confirmed the attached form was sent, and Brenda Juarez subsequently sent an additional message at 12:29 PM to acknowledge and sign off, with the standard confidentiality notice included in the email. Finally, at 3:12 PM (August 4, 2023, 15:12:56 -0500), Brenda clarified the cost details: the cost of the medication is $3,000.00 with no reduction, and she invited any questions at her phone number [PHONE-1728]). She noted that an updated approval form was attached and provided her contact information and the ASP Cares corporate office address for payments: ASP Cares, 13988 Diplomat Dr. Suite 100, Farmers Branch, TX 75234. The communications repeatedly included the standard confidentiality statements typical of these emails, indicating that the contents were intended solely for the addressee(s) and were confidential and privileged if applicable.

In summary, the main facts are: the patient Muhammad Alif’s prescription was identified as high-cost and requiring prior approval; the recommended billing approach was to bill Mr. Alif’s private health insurance; the medication was to be transferred to the patient’s local pharmacy; the established payments were to be sent to ASP Cares’ corporate office; and the updated LOP Rx Approval Form was attached in the communications. The documented cost of the medication was $3,000.00 with no reductions, and Brenda Juarez provided the final confirmation and contact details related to the approval and payment process.

item_398.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-1879]. The client is Muhammad Alif, associated with claim AP92071. This note summarizes the email communications between The Whaley Law Firm and West Bend Mutual Insurance regarding the case.

On June 20, 2023, Ashley Becerra, Senior Claims Representative for Casualty Claims at West Bend Mutual Insurance, sent an inquiry to the Whaley Law Firm asking for the initial ER records for Mr. Alif and requesting a status update on whether Mr. Alif is still treating and, if so, how he is being treated. The message included Becerra’s contact information and stated the West Bend address of 1900 South 18th Avenue, West Bend, WI 53095, with a toll-free number and direct lines for communication.

On June 21, 2023, at approximately 10:54 AM, Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers' Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, replied to Ashley. She stated that the records were attached and that she believes Mr. Alif has completed treatment, though she would need to verify that with Aaron.

Later the same day, June 21, 2023, at 12:20 PM and 21 seconds (Eastern Time, -0400), Sarena sent another email confirming that Aaron Whaley had been able to verify that Mr. Alif has completed treatment and that the demand is in the drafting process. Sarena advised that once the demand is completed, it would be forwarded to Ashley as soon as possible. She also invited Ashley to contact the firm to discuss any further questions in detail.

Sarena M. Tuttle’s signature block followed, identifying her role as Litigation Paralegal and Workers' Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222. Her direct and office phone numbers, as well as her email address, were listed: D [PHONE-1880]; O [PHONE-1881] ext 104; E Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note indicating the email address is new. The original message was sent from Sarena to Ashley Becerra, with Aaron Whaley CC’d on the email chain.

item_446.note: Case Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2070] involves client Muhammad Alif. In March 2023, the matter included a forwarded email thread titled “Fwd: Muhammad Alif Brain Testing Approval.” On March 14, 2023, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, forwarded this item to Aaron Whaley with the note “Another Request for Approval of Brain Mapping…,” and she included her firm contact details and a note to use her new email address Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com.

The forwarded thread contains a message from Axon Medical Centers Admin dated March 9, 2023, at 3:39 PM, with the subject “Muhammad Alif Brain Testing Approval.” The email is addressed to Muhammad Alif and to Dr. Allen Starkey ([EMAIL-2071]). It states that Axon Medical Centers are requesting approval for traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing for Muhammad Alif, who is a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD, a physician who is double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry and whose specialty includes physical medicine, rehabilitation, and sleep disorders. Dr. Hwang recommends two procedures prior to treatment: Brain Mapping and MRI/DTI. These tests are intended to better identify traumatic brain injury.

The TBI testing package, or battery, includes Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology for $8,000 and DTI/MRI for $8,000. The message invites the recipient to learn more about multifactorial testing via the link http://meet.ceostx.com and provides Dr. Matt DeGaetano’s contact at [EMAIL-2072] for direct discussion if scheduling is needed. The Indications section explains that Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology provide the most sophisticated, state-of-the-art, real-time imaging and brain training available, allowing visualization of live activity in the limbic system, anterior cingulate, fusiform gyrus, Brodmann areas, and more by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously. It notes that brain dysfunction can have a variety of causes, including encephalopathy, memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, and cognitive decline. For the DTI/MRI, the email describes diffusion tensor imaging as a technique that estimates the axonal (white matter) organization of the brain, with fiber tractography as a 3D reconstruction method to assess neural tracts using DTI data; it is a non-invasive imaging tool used to investigate white matter damaged during traumatic brain injury, even in the absence of neurological symptoms.

The message asks the recipient to reply with acceptance or denial and to attach a Letter of Protection (LOP) if testing is approved. The administration contact is Axon Medical Centers, which operates in Dallas, Houston, San Antonio, El Paso, and Austin, with a general phone number of [PHONE-2073]. The message also contains a standard confidentiality notice stating that the information in the transmission may be privileged and confidential, including patient information protected by federal and state privacy laws, and that it is intended only for the named recipients. If the recipient is not the intended person, review, dissemination, distribution, or duplication is prohibited, and the recipient should contact the sender at [EMAIL-2074] or [PHONE-2075] and destroy all copies of the original message.

An internal email titled “Muhammad Alif Brain Testing Approval” was sent from Axon Medical Centers Admin ([EMAIL-2078]) on March 9, 2023 at 12:38:58 PM Pacific Standard Time. The message was addressed to Muhammad Alif at sarena@whaleylawfirm.com and to Dr. Allen Starkey at [EMAIL-2079], with no listed recipients in CC.

In the body of the email, Axon Medical Centers requested approval for traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing for Muhammad Alif, who is a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD, a physician double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry, with a specialty in physical medicine, rehabilitation, and sleep disorders. Dr. Hwang recommends Brain Mapping and MRI/DTI prior to treatment. The TBI battery comprises Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology at $8,000 and the DTI/MRI at $8,000. The email provides a link (http://meet.ceostx.com) to schedule a time with Dr. Matt DeGaetano if the recipient would like to learn more about how multifactorial testing can identify brain injuries. If scheduling time is difficult or a direct conversation is preferred, the contact for Dr. DeGaetano is [EMAIL-2080]. 

Indications for Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology: described as the most sophisticated, state-of-the-art, real-time imaging/brain training available. The procedure visualizes live activity in the limbic system, anterior cingulate, fusiform gyrus, Brodmann areas, and more by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously. Brain dysfunction can have a variety of causes (encephalopathy) and may manifest as memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, and cognitive decline. Indications for DTI/MRI explain that diffusion tensor imaging is an MRI technique that uses anisotropic diffusion to estimate the axonal (white matter) organization of the brain, and that fiber tractography (FT) is a 3D reconstruction technique to assess neural tracts using data from diffusion tensor imaging. It is a non-invasive medical imaging tool used to investigate the structure of white matter that is damaged during a Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) without any neurological symptoms.

The sender requests a reply indicating acceptance or denial of the testing, and asks that a Letter of Protection (LOP) be attached if testing is approved. The message closes with the administration contact details for Axon Medical Centers, serving Dallas, Houston, San Antonio, El Paso, and Austin, at [PHONE-2081]. A confidentiality note follows, indicating that the transmission may contain privileged and confidential information, including patient information protected by federal and state privacy laws, and instructing unintended recipients to contact the sender and destroy all copies.

item_470.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2164]. Client: Muhammad Alif.

On February 13, 2023, at 3:20 PM, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm emailed Muhammad Alif regarding his PIP Payment Ledger. She stated that the ledger had been received in the mail, was attached, and listed the payments made by the PIP carrier. She noted that a $1,000 deductible was applied to the S&M Billing & Management invoices and that this would be discussed further during the negotiation phase of the claim. She provided a provider-by-provider breakdown: S&M Billing & Management billed $6,090.00 and was paid $3,865.00; Innovation Open MRI billed $3,200.00 and was paid $1,600.00; Lynn Family Vision & Training billed $485.00 and was paid $485.00; Partners in Physical Therapy billed $1,118.00 and was paid $838.00; Norton Leatherman Spine billed $305.00 and was paid $305.00. Additional bills listed included ParkRidge East Hospital ($5,673.40), Radiology Alliance ($458.00), Spring Creek Emergency Physicians ($1,707.00), Modern Chiropractic ($450.00), Mark Lynn & Associates ($300.00), and Aptiva Health ($1,475.00). She also noted that the PIP Adjuster had applied $7,093.00 in payments as listed, and that Muhammad currently has $14,168.40 in outstanding medical bills not including the $25,213.45 for Cutting Edge, Lynn Family Vision, and the KORT Physical Therapy that have not been submitted to Farmers at this time. She invited Muhammad to contact Aaron to discuss any questions in further detail and included her contact information and new email address.

At 4:04 PM the same day, Muhammad Alif replied to Serena, asking for clarification on whether all of these bills are for his first accident. He also mentioned that he would be released from chiropractic care very soon, but he continued to experience significant head pain and memory loss related to the first accident. He emphasized the importance of following doctors’ orders for his traumatic brain injury (TBI) treatment and added that he would be seeing a speech pathologist and would send information about his neurologist’s psychiatric treatment. He also noted that he had applied for health insurance and would share that information the following day.

At 4:08 PM, Sarena responded to Muhammad, clarifying that the Payment Ledger is for his first accident and that what appeared on the ledger is exactly what the providers had sent to Farmers.

Later that same day, at 6:23 PM, Muhammad replied again, stating that he understood which providers were being paid and asked whether the insurance company had been notified about these bills. He also reiterated that he would be seeing a speech pathologist and would provide information about his neurologist’s psychiatric treatment. He again noted that he had applied for health insurance and would have that information tomorrow.

On February 14, 2023, at 11:00:12 AM (Eastern Time), Sarena M. Tuttle sent another update to Muhammad and the other recipients. She explained that the information came from Muhammad’s PIP carrier, and that his BI carrier was aware of some—but not all—of the bills at that time. As discussed, they would request records and bills from all providers to ensure both sides have copies of all records and invoices. She requested that Muhammad provide his speech pathologist’s name and address as soon as possible so they could obtain those records and bills, noting that this information should be available to him on Norton MyChart. She congratulated him on applying for medical health insurance and cautioned that treatment before the coverage date can be denied, but that this situation would be reviewed and discussed in more detail during the claim negotiation phase. She invited Muhammad to contact them with any questions. The message included The Whaley Law Firm’s address—712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222—and direct lines: D [PHONE-2165], O [PHONE-2166] ext 104, E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note to use the new email address. The message was sent to Muhammad Alif ([EMAIL-2167]), Aaron Whaley ([EMAIL-2168]), Nona Bacote ([EMAIL-2169]), and Gail Sweasy ([EMAIL-2170]).

item_471.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2172]. Client: Muhammad Alif.

On February 14, 2023, Muhammad Alif ([EMAIL-2173]) sent an email to counsel at Whaley Law Firm (Aaron Whaley and Sarena Tuttle) with the subject “Re: Filing a lawsuit.” In the 9:38 AM message, he wrote from Yahoo Mail for iPad that he was very disturbed about the automobile accident cases and requested that the attorney file a lawsuit against harbor house, the owner of the commercial vehicle involved in accident number one. He stated it had been 90 days with no information on policy limits and asserted that insurance companies “like to play games,” asking the attorney to push the envelope to file a lawsuit.

That same day, at 1:58 PM, Aaron Whaley responded. He explained that he had spoken to the adjuster, who would not disclose policy limits because, in the adjuster’s words, “there is not a concern that this claim will exceed the limits.” He stated the policy is commercial and that they have sufficient limits, estimating at least $500,000, likely $1,000,000. Whaley advised that lawsuits can be pursued, but cautioned that they are not fast; if speed is the goal, a lawsuit is not the route. He noted that lawsuits are, however, certain and described his usual stance: he does not typically file a lawsuit unless there is some impasse—either a liability dispute or a dispute over value that exceeds the cost of litigation. He explained there might be merit in filing now if one of these disputes appears inevitable, but even if a suit is filed and the opposing side agrees with their approach, it does not guarantee avoidance of litigation. He warned that defense counsel would likely want to participate and conduct discovery and depositions. In summary, he said litigation is long and costly but can lead to an eventual resolution, while pre-litigation is shorter and cheaper but may still result in litigation. He concluded by saying he would leave the decision to the client based on this information.

Later that day, at 7:48 PM, Muhammad Alif replied: “Thank you, counselor for a speedy response. It’s no need for a lawsuit. I just had to have some information about the numbers.” This message was sent from Yahoo Mail for iPad.

The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information appears in the thread as follows: Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Ln, Louisville, KY 40222, [PHONE-2174].

item_472.note: This case, Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2176], involves client Muhammad Alif and concerns an automobile/motor vehicle accident. In a message dated February 14, 2023 at 13:57:56 -0500, attorney Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm responded to Muhammad Alif and to Sarena Tuttle regarding whether a lawsuit should be filed. Whaley explained that he had spoken with the adjuster, who was not disclosing policy limits because, in the adjuster’s words, “there is not a concern that this claim will exceed the limits.” The adjuster stated it is a commercial policy with sufficient limits, and Whaley assumed the insurer had at least $500,000, and likely $1,000,000. He offered to file a lawsuit if the client wished, but cautioned that lawsuits are not fast and, if pursued, are usually certain; they are not typically filed unless there is some impasse. Whaley noted there can be merit in filing if one of two disputes—liability or value enough to trigger litigation costs—appears inevitable. However, he did not consider the case to be at an impasse, stating that if a suit were filed, defense counsel would almost certainly engage and proceed with discovery, depositions, and related steps. In summary, he described litigation as long and costly but with eventual resolution, and pre-litigation as shorter and cheaper but with the risk of ending up in litigation anyway. He concluded by leaving the decision to the client based on this information.

Earlier that same day, at 9:38 AM, Muhammad Alif wrote to Counselor Whaley expressing significant concern about the automobile accident cases and requesting that a lawsuit be filed against Harbor House, described as the owner of the commercial vehicle in accident number one. He noted that it had been 90 days with no information on policy limits and indicated a belief that insurance companies like to “play games,” urging Whaley to push to file the lawsuit. The message was sent from Yahoo Mail for iPad. The note includes the signature block for Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm (712 Lyndon Ln, Louisville, KY 40222, [PHONE-2177]), indicating the communication style and contact details associated with the matter.

item_478.note: Case Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2196] concerns client Muhammad Alif. On February 13, 2023, Axon Medical Centers Admin, emailing from [EMAIL-2197], sent a message with the subject “Muhammed Alif Brain Testing Approval” to MUHAMMED ALIF at sarena@whaleylawfirm.com and to “Dr. Allen Starkey” at [EMAIL-2198]. The date and time on the message are Mon, 13 Feb 2023 06:45:06 -0800 (PST). The email requests approval for traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing for MUHAMMED ALIF, who is a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD, who is double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry and has a specialty in physical medicine, rehab, and sleep disorders. Dr. Hwang recommends the following procedures: oculomotor assessment, posturography, neurocognitive testing, brain mapping, and MRI/DTI prior to treatment. The TBI testing battery is itemized as follows: oculomotor assessment — $2,000; neurocognitive testing — $2,200; posturography — $500; brain mapping and electrophysiology — $8,000; and the DTI/MRI — $8,000. If you would like to learn more about how multifactorial testing is beneficial for identifying brain injuries, please click the link http://meet.ceostx.com to schedule a time to speak with Dr. Matt DeGaetano. If scheduling is difficult or you would like to speak with him directly, please contact [EMAIL-2199]. Indications for the tests are as follows: for oculomotor assessment, brain injury, headaches, fatigue, blurry vision, foggy thinking, reading difficulties, cognitive challenges, balance issues, trouble sleeping, and mood changes; blurred vision, double vision, nausea, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensation, and lightheadedness are also listed. For posturography, indications include brain injury, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensation, and lightheadedness. For neurocognitive testing, the assessment can help determine the areas of the brain impacted by a TBI and how these impairments affect day-to-day functioning; importantly, testing can also determine how factors such as depression, anxiety, and life stress are impacting cognitive functioning, memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, anxiety, and post-traumatic stress. For Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology, the note describes it as the most sophisticated, state-of-the-art, real-time imaging/brain training available, enabling visualization of live activity in the limbic system, anterior cingulate, fusiform gyrus, Brodmann areas, and more by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously; brain dysfunction can have various causes (encephalopathy), with symptoms including memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, and cognitive decline. For DTI/MRI, it explains that diffusion tensor imaging is an MRI technique using anisotropic diffusion to estimate the axonal (white matter) organization of the brain; fiber tractography (FT) is a 3D reconstruction technique to assess neural tracts using DTI data; this non-invasive imaging tool investigates the structure of white matter damaged during a TBI, even in the absence of neurological symptoms. 

Administration for Axon Medical Centers is listed as Dallas, Houston, San Antonio, El Paso, and Austin, with phone number [PHONE-2200]. The message also includes a standard privacy notice stating that the information in the transmission may contain privileged and confidential information, including patient information protected by federal and state privacy laws, and that it is intended only for the named recipient. If you are not the intended recipient, review, dissemination, distribution, or duplication is strictly prohibited, and you are asked to contact the sender at [EMAIL-2201] or [PHONE-2202] and destroy all copies. The email concludes with a request to reply back accepting or denying the requests, and to attach a LOP if testing is approved.

item_484.note: Case Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2223], client Muhammad Alif.

On February 13, 2023, at 10:42:01 a.m. Eastern Time, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm wrote to Nona Bacote regarding medical concerns. In her message, she thanked Muhammad for the appointment update and requested clarification on which speech pathologist was being referenced, noting that Norton Community Hospital is “not a proper location” and asking for the doctor’s name and address. She stated that, as discussed previously, they do not know the policy limits of the first accident and that the insurance company is not required to disclose this information. She added that they do not have a “patient ledger” for treatment to date and that they are still awaiting several sets of medical records and billing related to the treatment, with no providers paid to date to her knowledge. Regarding the demand package, she instructed that Muhammad would need to follow up with Aaron, explaining that a Demand Package cannot be sent until all medical records and bills have been obtained and treatment has been completed. She noted that she had updated the bodily injury adjuster with the medical records and bills on file, but emphasized that this was not a formal demand and no offers were made based on the information provided. She closed by inviting Muhammad to contact them with any further questions. The signature block identified Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s Louisville, Kentucky address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222), direct line [PHONE-2224], office line [PHONE-2225] ext 104, and email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, marked as the new address.

Nona Bacote replied on the same day, February 13, 2023, at 7:53 a.m. She began, “Good Morning Serena,” and explained that she had an appointment on Friday with Dr. Steven Patton, who referred her to a speech pathologist at Norton Community Hospital regarding her speech, and that she was waiting for the appointment date. She acknowledged that Aaron had already started working on the demand package for settlement and requested that Aaron be informed that a life-care plan should be considered with the demand package for medical costs and projection of other health concerns as needed. She also stated that for her second accident, she would have three MRI’s taken Tuesday in Lake Mary, Florida, as requested by Dr. William Hwang, MD, and that American Transit Insurance would be covering the bill. She noted that her team of doctors was very concerned about a life care planner for medical and rehabilitation care and asked who would pay for that associated cost if needed. Regarding both accidents, she asked whether any information had been obtained about policy limits and, if so, what those limits were for each accident. She also requested a patient ledger showing which doctors had been paid. The message concluded with her signature: “Thanks, Muhammad Alif.”

item_510.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2336]. Client: Muhammad Alif. The matter centers on two motor vehicle accidents and the medical treatment tied to them.

In an email thread dated February 6, 2023, Aaron Whaley of Whaley Law Firm asked Sarena Tuttle to clarify which accident Muhammad Alif treated for at Starlite, querying whether the facility was Stalite, Modern, or Tri-State Injury. He stated that he believed the first accident involved a traumatic brain injury (TBI) only, while the second involved a neck and back injury.

Sarena Tuttle replied later that same day, explaining that all of Muhammad Alif’s providers are documented and that records and bills have been requested and are awaiting receipt. Providers have a minimum of 30 days to produce these documents. She noted that policy limits and PIP information cannot be released to Starlite prior to submitting a demand, which cannot be submitted until all medical bills and records are received. She added that Aaron typically waits to review medical bills before releasing PIP payments so he can determine how the available benefits should be allocated among multiple providers, especially since over $30,000 had already been incurred between two of them. She indicated she had forwarded this information to him for review, along with the statement that a civil suit was being “following” or “filed” on Muhammad Alif’s behalf, and that he would reach out to discuss the matter further.

Earlier that day, Nona Bacote had sent a separate message seeking clarification of Muhammad Alif’s medical treatment related to the two accidents. She stated that, on November 8, 2023, Muhammad Alif was involved in his first accident and received treatment at Parkridge Medical Center, followed by care from Norton Health Care, Cutting Edge, Anointed Hands, Mark Lynn, and Kort Physical Therapy, in that order. All imaging had been performed at Innovative Open MRI & Imaging Diagnostic Imaging Center in Lake Mary, Florida, and he had a consultation with Aptiv. She noted that on Wednesday, February 8, 2023, he would be going to Mayo Clinic in Rochester, New York for additional treatment. Farmers Insurance was identified as the insurance company for this accident, and all bills were to be sent to them for payment from the listed treatment centers. She requested policy limits from Farmers immediately.

Bacote also stated that, on December 9, 2023, Muhammad Alif was involved in his second accident in New York, where his cab was rear-ended by another vehicle. He had been seen only by Cutting Edge and Starlite Chiropractor for medical treatment for this incident, and he had uninsured motorist insurance in relation to this claim. She acknowledged that the information was extensive and asked to be advised if it was too much to handle.

The email thread closes with Aaron Whaley’s signature from Whaley Law Firm.

item_516.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2368]
Client: Muhammad Alif

Re: Accidents

On February 6, 2023, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm emailed Nona Bacote, with Aaron Whaley and Muhammad Alif copied, to confirm that all of the client’s providers had been documented and that the client had confirmed this repeatedly. She stated that all medical records and bills had been requested and were being awaited, and that providers have a minimum of 30 days to produce these documents. The client expressed a desire for policy limits and PIP to be released to Starlite. Sarena explained that insurance companies are not required to disclose policy limits prior to a demand, and a demand cannot be submitted until all medical bills and records are received. She also explained that Aaron typically reviews the medical bills before releasing PIP payments, as he determines who receives what portion of the available benefits. He cannot release all benefits to a single provider when there are multiple providers and roughly $30,000 outstanding between two of them. She advised that she had forwarded this information to him for review, along with the statement that a civil suit is being “following” or “filed” on the client’s behalf, and that he would reach out to discuss the matter further.

On the same date, February 6, 2023 at 11:54 AM, Nona Bacote replied to Serena to clarify the client’s medical treatment in relation to the two accidents.

She stated that in the first accident, on November 8, 2023, the client received treatment at Parkridge Medical Center and subsequently received additional care from the following providers, listed in the order below: Norton Health Care (2nd), Cutting Edge (3rd), Anointed Hands (4th), Mark Lynn (5th), and Kort Physical Therapy (6th). All imaging was performed at Innovative Open MRI & Imaging Diagnostic Imaging Center in Lake Mary, Florida, and the client also received a Consultation at Aptiv. On Wednesday, February 8, 2023, the client would be going to Mayo Clinic in Rod Chester, New York for additional medical treatment.

Farmers Insurance is identified as the insurer for this accident only. All bills should be sent to Farmers for payment from the treatment centers listed above, and the client is requesting policy limits immediately from Farmers.

Regarding the second accident, on December 9, 2023 the client was involved in a second accident in New York, where she was in a cab that was rear-ended by another automobile. She has only been seen for medical treatment by Cutting Edge and Starlite Chiropractor. For this accident, she has uninsured motorist insurance.

The client acknowledged that this is a lot of information and asked to be notified if it is too much to handle. The note is signed by Muhamad Alif.

item_531.note: Case Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2425] involves client Muhammad Alif.

On February 1, 2023, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm forwarded an email titled MUHAMMED ALIF Brain Testing Approval to Aaron Whaley. The message, sent from Sarena’s address at sarena@whaleylawfirm.com, asked AW to approve the brain testing for MUHAMMED ALIF and included the Whaley Law Firm’s contact details: 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-2426]; O: [PHONE-2427] ext 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note indicating a new email address.

The forwarded chain contains a message from Cutting Edge Admin dated January 31, 2023, addressed to MUHAMMED ALIF. It states that approval is being requested for traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing for MUHAMMED ALIF, who is a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD, who is double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry and has specialty training in physical medicine, rehabilitation, and sleep disorders. Dr. Hwang recommends a battery of procedures including an oculomotor assessment, posturography, neurocognitive testing, brain mapping, and MRI/DTI prior to treatment, all intended to better identify traumatic brain injury.

The TBI testing battery includes the following components and costs: Oculomotor assessment ($2,000); Neurocognitive testing ($2,200); Posturography ($500); Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology ($8,000); and the DTI/MRI ($8,000). The message notes that additional information about how multifactorial testing can benefit the identification of brain injuries is available by visiting http://meet.ceostx.com to schedule a time to speak with Dr. Matt DeGaetano; if scheduling is difficult, or if there is a preference to speak with him directly, contact can be made at [EMAIL-2428].

Indications for the tests are detailed as follows: Oculomotor assessment is indicated for brain injury, headaches, fatigue, blurry vision, foggy thinking, reading difficulties, cognitive challenges, balance issues, trouble sleeping, mood changes, blurred vision, double vision, nausea, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensations, and lightheadedness. Posturography is indicated for brain injury, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensations, and lightheadedness. Neurocognitive testing can help determine the brain areas affected by a TBI and how these impairments impact day-to-day functioning, and it can also evaluate how other factors such as depression, anxiety, and life stress influence cognitive functioning, memory loss, concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, anxiety, and post-traumatic stress. Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology is described as the most sophisticated, state-of-the-art, real-time imaging/brain training available, allowing visualization of live activity in regions such as the Limbic system, anterior cingulate, fusiform gyrus, and Brodmann areas by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously; brain dysfunction can have various causes (encephalopathy) and can manifest as memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, and cognitive decline. DTI/MRI is explained as diffusion tensor imaging, an MRI technique that uses anisotropic diffusion to estimate the axonal (white matter) organization of the brain; fiber tractography is a 3D reconstruction technique to assess neural tracts using DTI data. It is a non-invasive medical imaging tool used to investigate white matter structure damaged during a Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) even in the absence of neurological symptoms.

Please reply back with acceptance or denial of the testing requests, and attach a Letter of Protection (LOP) if testing is approved.

item_532.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2430]. Client: Muhammad Alif.

A request for approval of traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing for MUHAMMED ALIF, a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD, who is double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry with a specialty in physical medicine, rehab, and sleep disorders, was sent on January 31, 2023. The requester noted that Dr. Hwang recommends the following procedures prior to treatment: an oculomotor assessment, posturography, neurocognitive testing, brain mapping with electrophysiology, and diffusion tensor imaging MRI (DTI/MRI). The TBI testing battery was itemized with costs as follows: oculomotor assessment - $2,000; neurocognitive testing - $2,200; posturography (this battery) - $500; brain mapping and electrophysiology - $8,000; and DTI/MRI - $8,000. The materials indicated that the tests are performed to better identify traumatic brain injury.

The submission included a note directing the recipient to learn more about the benefits of multifactorial testing by scheduling a time to speak with Dr. Matt DeGaetano at http://meet.ceostx.com, or, if time is limited, to contact him directly at [EMAIL-2431]. Indications associated with the tests were detailed as follows: for the oculomotor assessment, brain injury with headaches, fatigue, blurry vision, foggy thinking, reading difficulties, cognitive challenges, balance issues, trouble sleeping, mood changes, blurred or double vision, nausea, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensations, and lightheadedness; for posturography, brain injury with dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensations, and lightheadedness; for neurocognitive testing, a determination of the brain areas impacted by a TBI and how those impairments affect day-to-day functioning, including how factors such as depression, anxiety, and life stress influence cognitive functioning, memory loss, concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, anxiety, and post-traumatic stress; for brain mapping and electrophysiology, a description of this as the most sophisticated, real-time imaging/brain training available to visualize live activity in the limbic system and other regions by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously, with brain dysfunction having multiple potential causes (encephalopathy), including memory loss, concentration difficulties, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, and cognitive decline; and for DTI/MRI, an explanation of diffusion tensor imaging as an MRI technique that uses anisotropic diffusion to estimate axonal (white matter) organization, including fiber tractography as a 3D reconstruction technique to assess neural tracts, a non-invasive imaging tool to investigate white matter structure damaged during a TBI in the absence of neurological symptoms. The submission concluded with a request to reply accepting or denying the requests and to attach a Letter of Protection (LOP) if testing is approved.

The email thread shows that on February 1, 2023 at 5:59 PM, Sarena M. Tuttle (The Whaley Law Firm) wrote to AW with the question, “Hey AW, This came in on Mo. Approve?” Sarena’s signature block appeared with her address at The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, phone numbers D: [PHONE-2432] and O: [PHONE-2433] ext 104, and her new email address noted as Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com. The forwarded correspondence also includes the prior message from Cutting Edge Admin dated January 31, 2023 at 3:37 PM with the subject MUHAMMED ALIF Brain Testing Approval, addressed to MUHAMMED ALIF.

In response, on February 1, 2023 at 6:02 PM (Eastern Time), Aaron Whaley of the Whaley Law Firm replied, “Yes, approved.” The thread also contains an end-user signature block for Aaron Whaley, including his firm’s address at 712 Lyndon Ln, Louisville, KY 40222, and his phone number [PHONE-2434].

The correspondence is part of the Muhammed-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2435] case, with client Muhammad Alif, and documents the approval of the proposed TBI testing and associated procedures, the proposed providers, the cost structure, the educational materials and contact avenues for follow-up, and the instruction to attach an LOP upon approval.

item_533.note: Case Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2437] concerns client Muhammad Alif. In an email thread dated January 31, 2023, Cutting Edge Admin requested approval for traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing for MUHAMMED ALIF, who is a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD, described as double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry, with specialties in physical medicine, rehabilitation, and sleep disorders. Dr. Hwang recommended a testing battery including an oculomotor assessment, posturography, neurocognitive testing, brain mapping, and MRI/DTI prior to treatment in order to better identify a traumatic brain injury.

The requested TBI battery was itemized with the following components and fees: Oculomotor assessment for $2,000; Neurocognitive testing for $2,200; Posturography for $500; Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology for $8,000; and DTI/MRI for $8,000. Indications were provided for each test: the oculomotor assessment is indicated for brain injury symptoms such as headaches, fatigue, blurry or double vision, foggy thinking, reading difficulties, cognitive challenges, balance issues, trouble sleeping, mood changes, as well as blurred or nausea and dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensations, and lightheadedness. Posturography is indicated for brain injury with dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensations, and lightheadedness.

Neurocognitive testing was described as a means to determine the brain areas affected by TBI and how impairments impact day-to-day functioning, while also assessing how other factors such as depression, anxiety, and life stress influence cognitive functioning, memory, concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, anxiety, and post-traumatic stress. Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology were described as the most sophisticated, real-time imaging and brain training available, enabling visualization of live activity in regions including the Limbic system, anterior cingulate, fusiform gyrus, and Brodmann areas by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously, with brain dysfunction potentially arising from various causes (encephalopathy) and presenting as memory loss, difficulty concentrating, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, and cognitive decline. DTI/MRI was explained as diffusion tensor imaging that uses anisotropic diffusion to estimate the axonal (white matter) organization of the brain, with fiber tractography providing a 3D reconstruction to assess neural tracts, and described as a non-invasive imaging tool to investigate white matter damaged during TBI even in the absence of neurological symptoms. The request concluded with a directive to reply accepting or denying the requests and to attach a Letter of Protection (LOP) if testing is approved.

In response, on February 1, 2023, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, Louisville, KY, replied that the treatment had been approved by the attorney. She stated that the firm could not send a letter of protection or make agreements that may not be in the best interest of their client. However, she noted that the billing for the testing would be included in all damages presented for consideration at the time of negotiations. The message ended with an offer to provide further assistance and included her contact information: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct line (D) [PHONE-2438]; office line (O) [PHONE-2439] ext 104; email address Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note indicating this is a new email address. Signed by Sarena M. Tuttle, The Whaley Law Firm.

item_534.note: Case: Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2441]. Client: Muhammad Alif.

In the submission titled MUHAMMED ALIF Brain Testing Approval, dated January 31, 2023, Cutting Edge Admin sent a message to MUHAMMED ALIF (sarena@whaleylawfirm.com) regarding the brain testing needed for Muhammad Alif, a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD, who is double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry and has specialties in physical medicine, rehabilitation, and sleep disorders. The message requests approval for traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing and outlines the procedures Dr. Hwang recommends prior to treatment: an oculomotor assessment, posturography, neurocognitive testing, brain mapping, and MRI/DTI.

The TBI testing battery and their listed costs are as follows: oculomotor assessment ($2,000), neurocognitive testing ($2,200), posturography ($500), brain mapping and electrophysiology ($8,000), and DTI/MRI ($8,000). The note invites the recipient to learn more about how multifactorial testing can identify brain injuries by scheduling time to speak with Dr. Matt DeGaetano via http://meet.ceostx.com; if a time cannot be found or if direct contact is preferred, Dr. DeGaetano can be reached at [EMAIL-2442].

Indications for each component are detailed. Oculomotor assessment is indicated for brain injury, headaches, fatigue, blurry vision and foggy thinking, reading difficulties, cognitive challenges, balance issues, trouble sleeping, and mood changes, as well as blurred vision, double vision, nausea, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensation, and lightheadedness. Posturography is indicated for brain injury, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensation, and lightheadedness. Neurocognitive testing can help determine the brain areas affected by TBI and how these impairments impact day-to-day functioning; it can also reveal how other factors such as depression, anxiety, and life stress influence cognitive functioning, memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, anxiety, and post-traumatic stress. Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology is described as the most sophisticated, state-of-the-art, real-time imaging/brain training available, enabling visualization of live activity in regions such as the Limbic system, anterior cingulate, fusiform gyrus, and Brodmann areas by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously, with brain dysfunction having a variety of possible causes (encephalopathy) and associations with memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, and cognitive decline. DTI/MRI is described as diffusion tensor imaging—an MRI technique that uses anisotropic diffusion to estimate the axonal (white matter) organization of the brain; fiber tractography (FT) is a 3D reconstruction method to assess neural tracts using DTI data. This non-invasive imaging tool is used to investigate white matter structure that may be damaged during a Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) even in the absence of neurological symptoms.

Please reply with acceptance or denial of the requests. If testing is approved, please attach a Letter of Protection (LOP).

item_541.note: Case Muhammad-Alif-MVA-[DOB-2477] concerns the client Muhammad Alif, who was involved in a motor vehicle accident on November 8, 2022. The matter titled “Re: Full battery Brain Testing Approval” was discussed in communications dated January 24, 2023.

On January 24, 2023, the email thread shows that the case involves PIP coverage for Muhammad Alif with the same information as that used for Kendra Fogle, as well as PIP for the accident date of 11/08/22. The Farmers Insurance policy number is [PHONE-2478]-1-2, and the adjuster is Michael Santos, who can be reached at [PHONE-2479].

Earlier that day, at 5:22 PM, Cutting Edge Front Desk emailed a request for approval of traumatic brain injury (TBI) testing for MUHAMMED ALIF, who is a patient of Dr. William Hwang, MD. Dr. Hwang is double board-certified in neurology and psychiatry, with specialties in physical medicine, rehab, and sleep disorders. The desk note states that Dr. Hwang recommends the following procedures before treatment: Oculomotor assessment, Posturography, Neurocognitive testing, Brain Mapping, and MRI/DTI.

The TBI testing battery proposed includes the following components and costs: Oculomotor assessment at $2,000; Neurocognitive testing at $2,200; Posturography in this battery at $500; Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology at $8,000; and DTI/MRI at $8,000. The desk notice also invites learnings about multifactorial testing by directing the recipient to http://meet.ceostx.com to schedule time with Dr. Matt DeGaetano, and provides Dr. Matt DeGaetano’s direct contact as [EMAIL-2480].

Indications provided for each test are as follows:
- Oculomotor assessment: indications include brain injury, headaches, fatigue, blurry vision, foggy thinking, reading difficulties, cognitive challenges, balance issues, trouble sleeping, mood changes, blurred or double vision, nausea, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensation, and lightheadedness.
- Posturography: indications include brain injury, dizziness, balance problems, unsteadiness, falls, vertigo, spinning sensation, and lightheadedness.
- Neurocognitive testing: helps identify the brain areas impacted by a TBI and how impairments affect day-to-day functioning; it also clarifies how factors such as depression, anxiety, life stress, memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, anxiety, and post-traumatic stress influence cognitive functioning.
- Brain Mapping and Electrophysiology: described as the most sophisticated, state-of-the-art, real-time imaging/brain training available, enabling visualization of live activity in the Limbic system, anterior cingulate, fusiform gyrus, Brodmann areas, and more by recording 19 channels of brain activity simultaneously; brain dysfunction can have various causes (encephalopathy), including memory loss, lack of concentration, brain fog, irritability, forgetfulness, cognitive decline.
- DTI/MRI: diffusion tensor imaging is an MRI technique that uses anisotropic diffusion to estimate the axonal (white matter) organization of the brain, with fiber tractography (FT) as a 3D reconstruction to assess neural tracts; a non-invasive imaging tool to investigate white matter structure damaged during a TBI even in the absence of neurological symptoms.

The desk message concluded by requesting a response accepting or denying the testing, and asked that an LOP (letter of protection) be attached if the testing is approved.

The thread closing shows that at 6:00 PM on January 24, 2023, Aaron Whaley replied, “Yes, I approve.” The header of the original message is dated January 24, 2023, at 18:05:24 -0500, reflecting the same day approval in the thread.

Signature:
Aaron Whaley
Whaley Law Firm
712 Lyndon Ln, Louisville, KY 40222
Phone: [PHONE-2481]

Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222) wrote to Ashley Becerra regarding the letter of representation (LOR). She indicated she had reviewed the document and was not sure why the UM/UIM language had been inserted, and she attached an updated LOR for the file. Her new email address was noted as Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with the firm’s Louisville address and contact numbers.

In the days that followed, West Bend repeatedly requested a W-9 to add The Whaley Law Firm to their system. At 10:10 AM on November 29, 2022, Ashley responded that she needed the W-9 forwarded so she could have The Whaley Law Firm added to West Bend’s system. Earlier that same day, Sarena had requested the W-9 again and noted the attachment.

Messages on November 30, 2022 show ongoing communication about the liability decision and the correct contact details. At 8:43 AM, Ashley asked Sarena to clarify whose statement West Bend was still awaiting. Shortly thereafter, at 8:48 AM, Sarena reported that she had received a “kickback” from the email address provided for Ryan (Ryan Gorelick) and that [EMAIL-2734] had bounced the message, with [EMAIL-2735] being the intended recipient. Sarena’s signature included her firm information and note about a new email address. At 9:26 AM, Ashley stated that they were still pending a statement to finalize their liability decision, and at 9:43 AM she reiterated that Ryan Gorlick ([EMAIL-2736]) was the one handling the liability and property portions of the claim. By 9:45 AM, Sarena again thanked Ashley and asked for clarification on whose statement was still pending, reiterating the need for a liability decision. A later entry at 9:55 AM showed Ashley replying with a corrected email address for Ryan: [EMAIL-2737], and the message included Ashley’s full West Bend contact details.

Taken together, these communications show the following: The case involved a claim identified as AP92071 for Muhammad Alif arising from a motor vehicle incident on November 8, 2022 (MVA). On December 6, 2022, West Bend accepted 100% liability for Mr. Alif and notified Farmers Insurance that the PD portion of the claim was being handled by West Bend. A prior, multi-day email thread (November 22–30, 2022) between The Whaley Law Firm and West Bend’s Casualty Claims personnel revolved around the appropriate representation and liability decision, including discussions about updating the letter of representation due to UM/UIM language, requests for a W-9 to add The Whaley Law Firm to West Bend’s system, and ongoing clarification about which party’s statement was needed to finalize liability. Re: [External] Claim: AP92071 - Muhammad Alif

Overview
This matter involves the Whaley Law Firm representing Muhammad Alif in connection with an external claim, AP92071, related to a motor vehicle accident on November 8, 2022. The communications center on coordinating a liability decision and securing necessary representation documents, with West Bend Mutual Insurance (West Bend) handling liability and property portions of the claim and Ryan Gorlick ([EMAIL-2762]) involved in the liability decision process. Throughout the exchanges, the focus is on obtaining a pending liability statement necessary to finalize the liability determination and on ensuring the claims file is properly updated with the required W-9 information.

Chronology of communications

- November 22, 2022: Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm sent an email to Ashley Becerra regarding the letter of representation (LOR). Sarena noted that she had reviewed the document and was unsure why UM/UIM language had been inserted, and she attached an updated LOR for West Bend’s file. The message included the Whaley Law Firm’s contact details and stated that the updated LOR was attached for the file.

- November 28, 2022, 3:18 PM: Ashley Becerra of West Bend Mutual Insurance requested that The Whaley Law Firm forward a W-9 so the firm could be added to West Bend’s system.

- November 29, 2022, 9:45 AM: Sarena Tuttle replied, asking West Bend to contact their office to discuss the liability decision as soon as possible. She stated that a W-9 was attached in her previous message and reiterated the request to discuss the liability decision. She again provided the Whaley Law Firm’s contact information and noted the new email address.

- November 29, 2022, 10:10 AM: Ashley Becerra emailed again, requesting that the W-9 be forwarded so the firm could be added to West Bend’s system.

- November 29, 2022, 9:45 AM (sequence noted in the thread): The message from Sarena about the W-9 was circulated in the same day’s thread, indicating that the W-9 had been attached and urging discussion of the liability decision.

- November 29–30, 2022: Ongoing correspondence about the W-9 and the liability decision continued to appear in the thread. The West Bend side repeatedly indicated that a liability statement was outstanding, needed to finalize liability, and requested the appropriate representation and contact details. West Bend’s messages also included directions to contact Ryan Gorlick, who handles the liability and property portions of the claim.

- November 30, 2022, 9:43 AM: Ashley Becerra instructed contacting Ryan Gorlick ([EMAIL-2763]), who was handling the liability and property portions of the claim.

- November 30, 2022, 9:55 AM: Ashley Becerra reiterated the instruction to contact Ryan Gorlick, and Sarena asked for clarification about whose statement West Bend was awaiting. She noted they were approaching three weeks without a liability decision.

- November 30, 2022, 10:06 AM: Sarena Tuttle sent a follow-up, addressing Ashley and Ryan. She confirmed that Ashley had advised that the office was still pending a statement to make a liability decision and asked for clarification on whose statement was being awaited. She again stated that they were approaching three weeks without a decision and provided her contact details, including that her email address is the new one (Please note new email address).

- November 30, 2022, 9:45 AM (bounce notice): A delivery bounce occurred when attempting to email [EMAIL-2764] via [EMAIL-2765], indicating that the email address could not be found. A message stated: “Delivery has failed to these recipients or groups: [EMAIL-2766]. The email address you entered couldn't be found.” The bounce was documented with Sarena’s contact information and the note to try again or contact the email admin if the problem continued, with the signature indicating the new email address.

Additional details
- Throughout the thread, the subject remained: [External]Claim: AP92071 - Muhammad Alif.
- The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details are consistently listed as: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct line [PHONE-2767]; office line [PHONE-2768] ext 104; email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com; with a note to “PLEASE NOTE NEW EMAIL ADDRESS.”
- West Bend Mutual Insurance’s contact details appear as: 1900 South 18th Avenue, West Bend, WI 53095; toll-free [PHONE-2769] Ext 3631; phone [PHONE-2770]; fax [PHONE-2771]; email [EMAIL-2772]. The thread indicates that Ryan Gorlick is the point of contact for liability and property portions of the claim.
